<p><b>Sir Elton Hercules John</b> <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">CBE</a> (born <b>Reginald Kenneth Dwight</b>, 25 March 1947)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whoswho_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> is an English singer, songwriter, composer, pianist, record producer, and occasional actor. He has worked with lyricist <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Bernie Taupin</a> as his songwriter partner since 1967; they have collaborated on more than 30 albums to date.</p>
<p>In his five-decade career Elton John has sold more than 300 million records, making him one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> He has more than fifty <a href="/wiki/Top_40" title="Top 40">Top 40</a> hits, including seven consecutive No. 1 US albums, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">58 <i>Billboard</i> Top 40 singles, 27 Top 10</a>, four No. 2 and nine No. 1. For 31 consecutive years (1970–2000) he had at least one song in the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. His single "<a href="/wiki/Something_About_the_Way_You_Look_Tonight" title="Something About the Way You Look Tonight">Something About the Way You Look Tonight</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997</a>" sold over 33 million copies worldwide and is "the best-selling single of all time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSTO_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSTO-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guinness_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guinness-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> He has received six <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brit_Award" title="Brit Award">Brit Awards</a> – winning two awards for Outstanding Contribution to Music and the first Brits Icon in 2013 for his "lasting impact on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British culture</a>", an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Legend" title="Disney Legend">Disney Legend</a> award, and the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honors</a> in 2004. In 2004, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked him Number 49 on its list of 100 influential musicians of the rock and roll era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, <i>Billboard</i> ranked him the most successful male solo artist on "<a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_50th_Anniversary_Charts" title="Billboard Hot 100 50th Anniversary Charts">The <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 Top All-Time Artists</a>" (third overall).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Elton John was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1994, is an inductee into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songwriter%27s_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriter's Hall of Fame">Songwriter's Hall of Fame</a>, and is a fellow of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basca.org.uk_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basca.org.uk-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Having been named a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> in 1996, John received a <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of the United Kingdom">knighthood</a> from <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> for "services to music and charitable services" in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> John has performed at a number of royal events, such as the <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">funeral of Princess Diana</a> at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> in 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Party_at_the_Palace" title="Party at the Palace">Party at the Palace</a> in 2002 and the Queen's <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_Concert" title="Diamond Jubilee Concert">Diamond Jubilee Concert</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> in 2012.</p>
<p>He has been heavily involved in the fight against <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">AIDS</a> since the late 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992, he established the <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a> and a year later began hosting the annual <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation_Academy_Award_Party" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation Academy Award Party">Academy Award Party</a>, which has since become one of the highest-profile Oscar parties in the Hollywood film industry. Since its inception, the foundation has raised over $200 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundation_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foundation-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> John, who announced he was <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexual</a> in 1976 and has been openly gay since 1988, entered into a <a href="/wiki/Civil_partnership_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Civil partnership in the United Kingdom">civil partnership</a> with <a href="/wiki/David_Furnish" title="David Furnish">David Furnish</a> on 21 December 2005, and after gay marriage became legal in England, wed Furnish on 21 December 2014. He continues to be a champion for <a href="/wiki/LGBT_social_movements" title="LGBT social movements">LGBT social movements</a> worldwide and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h3>
<p>Elton John was born Reginald Kenneth Dwight on 25 March 1947, the eldest child of Stanley and only child of Sheila Eileen Dwight (née Harris),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> and was raised in <a href="/wiki/Pinner" title="Pinner">Pinner</a>, Middlesex in a <a href="/wiki/Council_house" title="Council house">council house</a> of his maternal grandparents. His parents did not marry until he was 6 years old, when the family moved to a nearby semi-detached house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> He was educated at Pinner Wood Junior School, Reddiford School and <a href="/wiki/Pinner_County_Grammar_School" title="Pinner County Grammar School">Pinner County Grammar School</a>, until age 17, when he left just prior to his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level" title="GCE Advanced Level">A Level</a> examinations to pursue a career in the music industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norman-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VisualDoc_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-VisualDoc-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When he began to seriously consider a career in music, Elton John's father, who served as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Lieutenant" title="Flight Lieutenant">Flight Lieutenant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, tried to steer him toward a more conventional career, such as banking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Norman-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> John has stated that his wild stage costumes and performances were his way of letting go after such a restrictive childhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VisualDoc_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-VisualDoc-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Both of John's parents were musically inclined, his father having been a trumpet player with the Bob Millar Band, a semi-professional big band that played at military dances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VisualDoc_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-VisualDoc-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The Dwights were keen record buyers, exposing John to the popular singers and musicians of the day, and John remembers being immediately hooked on rock and roll when his mother brought home records by <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Haley_%26_His_Comets" title="Bill Haley &amp; His Comets">Bill Haley &amp; His Comets</a> in 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Norman-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Elton John started playing the piano at the age of 3, and within a year, his mother heard him picking out <a href="/wiki/Winifred_Atwell" title="Winifred Atwell">Winifred Atwell</a>'s "The Skater's Waltz" by ear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norman_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-Norman-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> After performing at parties and family gatherings, at the age of 7 he took up formal piano lessons. He showed musical aptitude at school, including the ability to compose melodies, and gained some notoriety by playing like <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lee_Lewis" title="Jerry Lee Lewis">Jerry Lee Lewis</a> at school functions. At the age of 11, he won a junior scholarship to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music" title="Royal Academy of Music">Royal Academy of Music</a>. According to one of his instructors, John promptly played back, like a "gramophone record", a four-page piece by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Handel" title="Handel">Handel</a> that he heard for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg/220px-Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg/330px-Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg/440px-Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Academy_of_Music.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton studied at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music" title="Royal Academy of Music">Royal Academy of Music</a> in London for five years</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the next five years he attended Saturday classes at the Academy in central London, and has stated that he enjoyed playing <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Chopin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Bach</a> and singing in the choir during Saturday classes, but that he was not otherwise a diligent classical student.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> "I kind of resented going to the Academy", he says. "I was one of those children who could just about get away without practising and still pass, scrape through the grades."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> He even claims that he would sometimes skip classes and just ride around on <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">the Tube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> However, several instructors have testified that he was a "model student", and during the last few years he was taking lessons from a private tutor in addition to his classes at the Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-7"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Elton John's mother, though also strict with her son, was more vivacious than her husband, and something of a free spirit. With Stanley Dwight uninterested in his son and often physically absent, John was raised primarily by his mother and maternal grandmother. When his father was home, the Dwights would have terrible arguments that greatly distressed their son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-8"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> When John was 14, they divorced. His mother then married a local painter, Fred Farebrother, a caring and supportive stepfather whom John affectionately referred to as "Derf", his first name in reverse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-9"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> They moved into flat No. 1A in an eight-unit apartment building called Frome Court, not far from both previous homes. It was there that John would write the songs that would launch his career as a rock star; he would live there until he had four albums simultaneously in the American Top 40.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pub_pianist_to_staff_songwriter_.281962.E2.80.931969.29">Pub pianist to staff songwriter (1962–1969)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bluesology" title="Bluesology">Bluesology</a></div>
<p>At the age of 15, with the help of his mother and stepfather, Reginald Dwight became a weekend pianist at a nearby pub, the Northwood Hills Hotel, playing Thursday to Sunday nights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Known simply as "Reggie", he played a range of popular standards, including songs by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Reeves" title="Jim Reeves">Jim Reeves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a>, as well as songs he had written himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Costello_interview_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Costello_interview-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> A stint with a short-lived group called the Corvettes rounded out his time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-10"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1964, Dwight and his friends formed a band called <a href="/wiki/Bluesology" title="Bluesology">Bluesology</a>. By day, he ran errands for a music publishing company; he divided his nights between solo gigs at a London hotel bar and working with Bluesology. By the mid-1960s, Bluesology was backing touring American <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> musicians like <a href="/wiki/The_Isley_Brothers" title="The Isley Brothers">The Isley Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Major_Lance" title="Major Lance">Major Lance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labelle" title="Labelle">Patti LaBelle and The Bluebelles</a>. In 1966, the band became musician <a href="/wiki/Long_John_Baldry" title="Long John Baldry">Long John Baldry</a>'s supporting band, and played 16 times at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Marquee_Club" title="The Marquee Club">The Marquee Club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnPiano.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1668" data-file-width="2396" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/EltonJohnPiano.jpg/220px-EltonJohnPiano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/EltonJohnPiano.jpg/330px-EltonJohnPiano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/EltonJohnPiano.jpg/440px-EltonJohnPiano.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnPiano.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 1910 piano on which Elton John composed his first five albums, including his first hit single, "<a href="/wiki/Your_Song" title="Your Song">Your Song</a>"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1967, Dwight answered an advertisement in the British magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">New Musical Express</a></i>, placed by <a href="/wiki/Ray_Williams_(producer)" title="Ray Williams (producer)">Ray Williams</a>, then the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%26R" title="A&amp;R">A&amp;R</a> manager for <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Records" title="Liberty Records">Liberty Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bilb_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-bilb-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> At their first meeting, Williams gave Dwight a stack of lyrics written by <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Bernie Taupin</a>, who had answered the same ad. Dwight wrote music for the lyrics, and then mailed it to Taupin, beginning a partnership that still continues<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Elton_John&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. When the two first met in 1967 they recorded what would become the first Elton John/Bernie Taupin song: "Scarecrow". Six months later Dwight was going by the name "Elton John" in homage to Bluesology saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Elton_Dean" title="Elton Dean">Elton Dean</a> and Long John Baldry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Costello_interview_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Costello_interview-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The team of Elton John and Bernie Taupin joined <a href="/wiki/Dick_James" title="Dick James">Dick James</a>'s <a href="/wiki/DJM_Records" title="DJM Records">DJM Records</a> as staff songwriters in 1968, and over the next two years wrote material for various artists, like <a href="/wiki/Roger_Cook_(songwriter)" title="Roger Cook (songwriter)">Roger Cook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lulu_(singer)" title="Lulu (singer)">Lulu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vinita_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vinita-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Taupin would write a batch of lyrics in under an hour and give it to John, who would write music for them in half an hour, disposing of the lyrics if he couldn't come up with anything quickly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vinita_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vinita-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> For two years, they wrote <a href="/wiki/Easy_listening" title="Easy listening">easy-listening</a> tunes for James to peddle to singers. Their early output included a contender for the UK entry for the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> in 1969, for Lulu, called "I Can't Go On (Living Without You)". It came <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_1969" title="United Kingdom in the Eurovision Song Contest 1969">sixth</a> of six songs. In 1969, John provided piano for <a href="/wiki/Roger_Hodgson" title="Roger Hodgson">Roger Hodgson</a> on his first released single, "Mr. Boyd" by Argosy, a quartet that was completed by <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Quaye" title="Caleb Quaye">Caleb Quaye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Olsson" title="Nigel Olsson">Nigel Olsson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton John was also a session musician for other artists including playing piano on <a href="/wiki/The_Hollies" title="The Hollies">The Hollies</a>' "<a href="/wiki/He_Ain%27t_Heavy,_He%27s_My_Brother" title="He Ain't Heavy, He's My Brother">He Ain't Heavy, He's My Brother</a>" and singing backing vocals for <a href="/wiki/The_Scaffold" title="The Scaffold">The Scaffold</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Debut_album_to_Goodbye_Yellow_Brick_Road_.281969.E2.80.931973.29">Debut album to <i>Goodbye Yellow Brick Road</i> (1969–1973)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_on_stage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Elton_John_on_stage.jpg/220px-Elton_John_on_stage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Elton_John_on_stage.jpg/330px-Elton_John_on_stage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Elton_John_on_stage.jpg/440px-Elton_John_on_stage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_on_stage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John on stage in 1971</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the advice of music publisher Steve Brown, John and Taupin started writing more complex songs for John to record for DJM. The first was the single "I've Been Loving You" (1968), produced by <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Quaye" title="Caleb Quaye">Caleb Quaye</a>, former Bluesology guitarist. In 1969, with Quaye, drummer Roger Pope, and bassist Tony Murray, John recorded another single, "<a href="/wiki/Lady_Samantha" title="Lady Samantha">Lady Samantha</a>", and an album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empty_Sky_(album)" title="Empty Sky (album)">Empty Sky</a></i>.</p>
<p>For their follow-up album, <i><a href="/wiki/Elton_John_(album)" title="Elton John (album)">Elton John</a></i>, Elton John and Bernie Taupin enlisted <a href="/wiki/Gus_Dudgeon" title="Gus Dudgeon">Gus Dudgeon</a> as producer and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Buckmaster" title="Paul Buckmaster">Paul Buckmaster</a> as <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">musical arranger</a>. <i>Elton John</i> was released in April 1970 on DJM Records/<a href="/wiki/Pye_Records" title="Pye Records">Pye Records</a> in the UK and <a href="/wiki/Uni_Records" title="Uni Records">Uni Records</a> in the US, and established the formula for subsequent albums – gospel-chorded rockers and poignant ballads. The first single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Border_Song" title="Border Song">Border Song</a>", made into the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">US Top 100</a>, peaking at Number 92. The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Your_Song" title="Your Song">Your Song</a>", reached number seven in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> and number eight in the US, becoming John's first hit single as a singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The album soon became his first hit album, reaching number four on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and number five on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Backed by ex-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spencer_Davis_Group" title="Spencer Davis Group">Spencer Davis Group</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Olsson" title="Nigel Olsson">Nigel Olsson</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Dee_Murray" title="Dee Murray">Dee Murray</a>, Elton John's first American concert took place at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Troubadour_(Los_Angeles)" title="The Troubadour (Los Angeles)">The Troubadour</a> in Los Angeles in August 1970, and was a success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The concept album <i><a href="/wiki/Tumbleweed_Connection" title="Tumbleweed Connection">Tumbleweed Connection</a></i> was released in October 1970, and reached number two in the UK and number five in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The live album <i><a href="/wiki/17-11-70" title="17-11-70">17-11-70</a></i> (<i>11–17–70</i> in the US) was recorded at a live show aired from A&amp;R Studios on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WABC-FM" title="WABC-FM">WABC-FM</a> in New York City. Sales of the live album were heavily hit in the US when an east coast <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">bootlegger</a> released the performance several weeks before the official album, including all 60 minutes of the aircast, not just the 40 minutes selected by Dick James Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1164" data-file-width="1870" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg/220px-Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg/330px-Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg/440px-Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_1972_1603720019.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John at the <a href="/wiki/Laeiszhalle" title="Laeiszhalle">Musikhalle</a>, Hamburg, in March 1972</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>John and Taupin then wrote the soundtrack to the obscure film <i><a href="/wiki/Friends_(1971_film)" title="Friends (1971 film)">Friends</a></i> and then the album <i><a href="/wiki/Madman_Across_the_Water" title="Madman Across the Water">Madman Across the Water</a></i>, the latter reaching number eight in the US and producing the hit songs, "<a href="/wiki/Levon_(song)" title="Levon (song)">Levon</a>", and the album's opening track "<a href="/wiki/Tiny_Dancer" title="Tiny Dancer">Tiny Dancer</a>". In 1972, <a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnstone" title="Davey Johnstone">Davey Johnstone</a> joined the <b>Elton John Band</b> on guitar and backing vocals. Released in 1972, <i><a href="/wiki/Honky_Ch%C3%A2teau" title="Honky Château">Honky Château</a></i> became John's first US number one album, spending five weeks at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, and began a streak of seven consecutive US number one albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The album reached number two in the UK, and spawned the hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Rocket_Man_(song)" title="Rocket Man (song)">Rocket Man (I Think It's Going To Be A Long, Long Time)</a>" (which is often compared to <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Space_Oddity_(song)" title="Space Oddity (song)">Space Oddity</a>") and "<a href="/wiki/Honky_Cat" title="Honky Cat">Honky Cat</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> both of which were recorded at <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">Trident Studios</a> in London.</p>
<p>The pop album <i><a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Shoot_Me_I%27m_Only_the_Piano_Player" title="Don't Shoot Me I'm Only the Piano Player">Don't Shoot Me I'm Only the Piano Player</a></i> came out at the start of 1973, and reached number one in the UK, the US, Australia among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The album produced the hits "<a href="/wiki/Crocodile_Rock" title="Crocodile Rock">Crocodile Rock</a>", his first US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> number one, and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daniel_(song)" title="Daniel (song)">Daniel</a>"; number two US, number four UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Both the album and "Crocodile Rock" were the first album and single, respectively on the consolidated <a href="/wiki/MCA_Records" title="MCA Records">MCA Records</a> label in the US, replacing MCA's other labels including Uni.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Goodbye_Yellow_Brick_Road" title="Goodbye Yellow Brick Road">Goodbye Yellow Brick Road</a></i>, released in October 1973, gained instant critical acclaim and topped the chart on both sides of the Atlantic, remaining at number one for two months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redbeard_GYBR_interview_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Redbeard_GYBR_interview-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> It also temporarily established John as a <a href="/wiki/Glam_rock" title="Glam rock">glam rock</a> star. It contained the US number 1 "<a href="/wiki/Bennie_and_the_Jets" title="Bennie and the Jets">Bennie and the Jets</a>", along with other hits, "<a href="/wiki/Goodbye_Yellow_Brick_Road_(song)" title="Goodbye Yellow Brick Road (song)">Goodbye Yellow Brick Road</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind" title="Candle in the Wind">Candle in the Wind</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night%27s_Alright_for_Fighting" title="Saturday Night's Alright for Fighting">Saturday Night's Alright for Fighting</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Funeral_for_a_Friend/Love_Lies_Bleeding" title="Funeral for a Friend/Love Lies Bleeding">Funeral for a Friend/Love Lies Bleeding</a>". <i>Goodbye Yellow Brick Road</i> is included in the <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> <a href="/wiki/Classic_Albums" title="Classic Albums">Classic Albums</a> series, discussing the making, recording, and popularity of the album through concert and home video footage including interviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Rocket_Record_Company_to_21_at_33_.281974.E2.80.931979.29">The Rocket Record Company to <i>21 at 33</i> (1974–1979)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="800" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elton_John.jpg/220px-Elton_John.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elton_John.jpg/330px-Elton_John.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Elton_John.jpg/440px-Elton_John.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton on the piano during a live performance in 1975</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>John formed his own MCA-distributed label named <a href="/wiki/The_Rocket_Record_Company" title="The Rocket Record Company">The Rocket Record Company</a> and signed acts to it – notably <a href="/wiki/Neil_Sedaka" title="Neil Sedaka">Neil Sedaka</a> ("Bad Blood", on which he sang background vocals) and <a href="/wiki/Kiki_Dee" title="Kiki Dee">Kiki Dee</a> – in which he took a personal interest. Instead of releasing his own records on Rocket, he opted for $8 million offered by MCA. When the contract was signed in 1974, MCA reportedly took out a $25 million insurance policy on John's life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1974 MCA released his <i><a href="/wiki/Elton_John%27s_Greatest_Hits" title="Elton John's Greatest Hits">Greatest Hits</a></i> album, a UK and US number one which is <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification#RIAA_Diamond_certifications_as_of_October_5.2C_2012" title="RIAA certification">certified Diamond</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> for sales of 16 million copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-5"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1974 a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> took place, resulting in Lennon appearing on Elton John's single cover of The Beatles' "<a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds</a>", the b-side of which was Lennon's "One Day at a Time." In return, John was featured on "<a href="/wiki/Whatever_Gets_You_thru_the_Night" title="Whatever Gets You thru the Night">Whatever Gets You thru the Night</a>" on Lennon's <i><a href="/wiki/Walls_and_Bridges" title="Walls and Bridges">Walls and Bridges</a></i> album. Later that year in what would be Lennon's last major live performance, the pair performed these two number 1 hits along with the Beatles classic "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>" at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York. Lennon made the rare stage appearance with John and his band to keep the promise he made that he would appear on stage with him if "Whatever Gets You Thru The Night" became a US number one single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Caribou_(album)" title="Caribou (album)">Caribou</a></i> was released in 1974 and became John's third number one in the UK, and topped the charts in the US, Canada and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-6"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artists.letssingit.com_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-artists.letssingit.com-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Reportedly recorded in two weeks between live appearances, it featured "<a href="/wiki/The_Bitch_Is_Back" title="The Bitch Is Back">The Bitch Is Back</a>" and the orchestrated "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Let_the_Sun_Go_Down_on_Me" title="Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me">Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artists.letssingit.com_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-artists.letssingit.com-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Step_into_Christmas" title="Step into Christmas">Step into Christmas</a>" was released as a stand-alone single in November 1973, and appears in the album's 1995 remastered re-issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="916" data-file-width="718" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG/220px-Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG/330px-Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG/440px-Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_john_cher_show_1975.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Performing in 1975, Elton often wore elaborate stage costumes on stage</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a> asked John to play a character called the "Local Lad" in the film of the rock opera <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tommy_(rock_opera)" title="Tommy (rock opera)">Tommy</a></i>, and to perform the song "<a href="/wiki/Pinball_Wizard" title="Pinball Wizard">Pinball Wizard</a>". Drawing on <a href="/wiki/Power_chord" title="Power chord">power chords</a>, John's version was recorded and used for the movie release in 1975 and the single came out in 1976 (1975 in the US). The song charted at number 7 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-7"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bally_Technologies" title="Bally Technologies">Bally</a> subsequently released a "Captain Fantastic" pinball machine featuring an illustration of John in his movie guise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hombach_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hombach-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 1975 autobiographical album <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Fantastic_and_the_Brown_Dirt_Cowboy" title="Captain Fantastic and the Brown Dirt Cowboy">Captain Fantastic and the Brown Dirt Cowboy</a></i> debuted at number one in the US, the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200#Additional_milestones" title="Billboard 200">first album ever</a> to do so, and stayed at the top for seven weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-record-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton John revealed his previously ambiguous personality on the album, with Taupin's lyrics describing their early days as struggling songwriters and musicians in London. The lyrics and accompanying photo booklet are infused with a specific sense of place and time that is otherwise rare in his music. "<a href="/wiki/Someone_Saved_My_Life_Tonight" title="Someone Saved My Life Tonight">Someone Saved My Life Tonight</a>" was the hit single from this album and captured an early turning point in Elton John's life. The album's release signalled the end of the Elton John Band, as an unhappy and overworked John dismissed Olsson and Murray, two people who had contributed much of the band's signature sound and who had helped build his live following since the beginning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hombach_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hombach-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circus_Magazine" title="Circus Magazine">Circus Magazine</a></i>, a spokesman for John Reid said the decision was reached mutually via phone while John was in Australia promoting <i>Tommy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raves_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-raves-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> She said there was no way Reid could have fired them "because the band are not employed by John Reid, they're employed by Elton John."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raves_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-raves-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> She went on to say Nigel would be going back to his solo work and Dee would do session work "and possibly cut a solo album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raves_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-raves-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Davey Johnstone and Ray Cooper were retained, Quaye and Roger Pope returned, and the new bassist was Kenny Passarelli; this rhythm section provided a heavier-sounding backbeat. <a href="/wiki/James_Newton_Howard" title="James Newton Howard">James Newton Howard</a> joined to arrange in the studio and to play keyboards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elton_Band_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elton_Band-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 1975, John introduced the line-up before a crowd of 75,000 in London's <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elton_Band_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elton_Band-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="800" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg/220px-Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg/330px-Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg/440px-Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_nel_1975.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John during a <i>Captain Fantastic</i> concert in 1975</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The rock-oriented <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_of_the_Westies" title="Rock of the Westies">Rock of the Westies</a></i> entered the US albums chart at number 1 like <i>Captain Fantastic</i>, a previously unattained feat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-record_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-record-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton John's stage wardrobe now included <a href="/wiki/Ostrich" title="Ostrich">ostrich</a> feathers, $5,000 spectacles that spelled his name in lights, and dressing up like the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Duck" title="Donald Duck">Donald Duck</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozart" title="Mozart">Mozart</a>, among others, at his concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1975, Elton received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HWOF_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-HWOF-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To celebrate five years since he first appeared at the venue, in 1975 Elton John played a two-night, four-show stand at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Troubadour_(Los_Angeles)" title="The Troubadour (Los Angeles)">The Troubadour</a>. With seating limited to under 500 per show, the chance to purchase tickets was determined by a postcard lottery, with each winner allowed two tickets. Everyone who attended the performances received a hardbound "yearbook" of the band's history. That year he also played piano on <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Ayers" title="Kevin Ayers">Kevin Ayers</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Sweet_Deceiver" title="Sweet Deceiver">Sweet Deceiver</a></i>, and was among the first and few white artists to appear on the black music series <i><a href="/wiki/Soul_Train" title="Soul Train">Soul Train</a></i> on American television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redbeard_GYBR_interview_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Redbeard_GYBR_interview-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> On 9 August 1975, John was named the outstanding rock personality of the year at the first annual Rock Music Awards at ceremonies held in Santa Monica, California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1976, the live album <i><a href="/wiki/Here_and_There_(Elton_John_album)" title="Here and There (Elton John album)">Here and There</a></i> was released in May, followed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Moves" title="Blue Moves">Blue Moves</a></i> album in October, which contained the single "<a href="/wiki/Sorry_Seems_to_Be_the_Hardest_Word" title="Sorry Seems to Be the Hardest Word">Sorry Seems to Be the Hardest Word</a>". His biggest success in 1976 was "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Go_Breaking_My_Heart" title="Don't Go Breaking My Heart">Don't Go Breaking My Heart</a>", a duet with Kiki Dee that topped both the UK and US charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-8"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Charts_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Charts-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, in an interview with <i>Rolling Stone</i> that year entitled "Elton's Frank Talk", John stated that he was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="424" data-file-width="600" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Elton_John_1.jpg/220px-Elton_John_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Elton_John_1.jpg/330px-Elton_John_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Elton_John_1.jpg/440px-Elton_John_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton performing live with <a href="/wiki/Ray_Cooper" title="Ray Cooper">Ray Cooper</a> in Dublin, Ireland in 1979</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides being the most commercially successful period, 1970–1976 is also held in the most regard critically. Within only a three-year span, between 1972 and 1975 John saw seven consecutive albums reach number one in the US, which had not been accomplished before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Redbeard_GYBR_interview_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Redbeard_GYBR_interview-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the six Elton John albums to make <i>Rolling Stone</i> '​s list of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>" in 2003, all are from this period, with <i>Goodbye Yellow Brick Road</i> ranked highest at number 91; similarly, the three Elton John albums given five stars by Allmusic (<i>Tumbleweed Connection</i>, <i>Honky Château</i>, and <i>Captain Fantastic</i>) are all from this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the same period, he made a guest appearance on the popular <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Morecambe_%26_Wise_Show_(1968%E2%80%931977)" title="The Morecambe &amp; Wise Show (1968–1977)">Morecambe and Wise Show</a></i> on the BBC. The two comics spent the episode pointing him in the direction of everywhere except the stage in order to prevent him singing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1977 Elton John announced he was retiring from performing; Taupin began collaborating with others. Now only producing one album a year, John issued <i><a href="/wiki/A_Single_Man_(album)" title="A Single Man (album)">A Single Man</a></i> in 1978, employing a new lyricist, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Osborne" title="Gary Osborne">Gary Osborne</a>; the album produced no singles that made the top 20 in the US but the two singles from the album released in the UK, "<a href="/wiki/Part-Time_Love" title="Part-Time Love">Part-Time Love</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Song_for_Guy" title="Song for Guy">Song for Guy</a>", both made the top 20 in the UK with the latter reaching the top 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-9"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1979, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Ray_Cooper" title="Ray Cooper">Ray Cooper</a>, Elton John became one of the first Western artists to tour the Soviet Union, as well as one of the first in Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> John returned to the US top ten with "<a href="/wiki/Mama_Can%27t_Buy_You_Love" title="Mama Can't Buy You Love">Mama Can't Buy You Love</a>" (number 9), a song originally rejected in 1977 by MCA before being released, recorded in 1977 with Philadelphia soul producer <a href="/wiki/Thom_Bell" title="Thom Bell">Thom Bell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> John reported that Thom Bell was the first person to give him voice lessons; Bell encouraged John to sing in a lower register. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disco_music" title="Disco music">disco</a>-influenced album, <i><a href="/wiki/Victim_of_Love_(album)" title="Victim of Love (album)">Victim of Love</a></i>, was poorly received. In 1979, John and <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Taupin</a> reunited, though they did not collaborate on a full album until 1983's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Too_Low_For_Zero" title="Too Low For Zero">Too Low For Zero</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/21_at_33" title="21 at 33">21 at 33</a></i>, released the following year, was a significant career boost, aided by his biggest hit in four years, "<a href="/wiki/Little_Jeannie" title="Little Jeannie">Little Jeannie</a>" (number 3 US), with the lyrics written by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Osborne" title="Gary Osborne">Gary Osborne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s:_The_Fox_to_Sleeping_with_the_Past_.281980.E2.80.931989.29">1980s: <i>The Fox</i> to <i>Sleeping with the Past</i> (1980–1989)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg/220px-Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg/330px-Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg/440px-Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_in_1980s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John performing in the 1980s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>His 1981 album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fox_(Elton_John_album)" title="The Fox (Elton John album)">The Fox</a></i>, was recorded in part during the same sessions as <i><a href="/wiki/21_at_33" title="21 at 33">21 at 33</a></i>, and also included collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Tom_Robinson" title="Tom Robinson">Tom Robinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judie_Tzuke" title="Judie Tzuke">Judie Tzuke</a>. On 13 September 1980, Elton John, with Olsson and Murray back in the Elton John Band, performed a free concert to an estimated 400,000 fans on The Great Lawn in <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> His 1982 hit "<a href="/wiki/Empty_Garden_(Hey_Hey_Johnny)" title="Empty Garden (Hey Hey Johnny)">Empty Garden (Hey Hey Johnny)</a>", came from his <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jump_Up!" title="Jump Up!">Jump Up!</a></i> album, his second under a new US recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>.</p>
<p>With original band members Johnstone, Murray and Olsson together again, he was able to return to the charts with the 1983 hit album <i><a href="/wiki/Too_Low_for_Zero" title="Too Low for Zero">Too Low for Zero</a></i>, which included "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Still_Standing" title="I'm Still Standing">I'm Still Standing</a>" (No. 4 UK) and "<a href="/wiki/I_Guess_That%27s_Why_They_Call_It_the_Blues" title="I Guess That's Why They Call It the Blues">I Guess That's Why They Call It the Blues</a>", the latter of which featured <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a> on harmonica and reached No. 4 in the US and No. 5 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-10"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Charts_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Charts-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 1983, Elton John caused controversy when he broke the United Nations' cultural boycott on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" title="Apartheid in South Africa">apartheid</a> South Africa by performing at the <a href="/wiki/Sun_City,_North_West" title="Sun City, North West">Sun City</a> venue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> He married his close friend and sound engineer, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renate_Blauel" title="Renate Blauel">Renate Blauel</a>, on Valentine's Day 1984 – the marriage lasted three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_costume.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Elton_John_costume.jpg/220px-Elton_John_costume.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Elton_John_costume.jpg/330px-Elton_John_costume.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Elton_John_costume.jpg/440px-Elton_John_costume.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_costume.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John costume from the 1986 <a href="/wiki/Tour_De_Force_(tour)" title="Tour De Force (tour)">Tour de Force</a> Australian concerts, on display in the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe" title="Hard Rock Cafe">Hard Rock Cafe</a>, London</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1985, he was one of the many performers at <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> held at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CLD_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-CLD-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> John played "Bennie and the Jets" and "Rocket Man"; then "Don't Go Breaking My Heart" with Kiki Dee for the first time since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Odeon" title="Hammersmith Odeon">Hammersmith Odeon</a> on 24 December 1982; and introduced his friend <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, still then of <a href="/wiki/Wham!" title="Wham!">Wham!</a>, to sing "Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CLD_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-CLD-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1985 he released <i><a href="/wiki/Breaking_Hearts" title="Breaking Hearts">Breaking Hearts</a></i> which featured the hit song "<a href="/wiki/Sad_Songs_(Say_So_Much)" title="Sad Songs (Say So Much)">Sad Songs (Say So Much)</a>", No. 5 in the US and No. 7 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-11"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton John also recorded material with <a href="/wiki/Millie_Jackson" title="Millie Jackson">Millie Jackson</a> in 1985. In 1986, he played the piano on two tracks on the <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Saxon_(band)" title="Saxon (band)">Saxon's</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_the_Nations" title="Rock the Nations">Rock the Nations</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A <i><a href="/wiki/Biography_(TV_series)" title="Biography (TV series)">Biography</a></i> channel special detailed the loss of Elton's voice in 1986 while on tour in Australia. Shortly thereafter he underwent throat surgery, which permanently altered his voice. Several non-cancerous polyps were removed from his vocal cords, resulting in a change in his singing voice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1987 he won a libel case against <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> which published false allegations of sex with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rent_boys" title="Rent boys">rent boys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1988, he performed five sold-out shows at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York, giving him 26 for his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Netting over $20 million, 2,000 items of Elton John's memorabilia were auctioned off at Sotheby's in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He placed other hits throughout the 1980s, including "<a href="/wiki/Nikita_(song)" title="Nikita (song)">Nikita</a>" which featured in a music video directed by <a href="/wiki/Ken_Russell" title="Ken Russell">Ken Russell</a>, No. 3 in the UK and No. 7 in the US in 1986, a live orchestral version of "Candle in the Wind", No. 6 in the US, and "<a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Wanna_Go_on_with_You_Like_That" title="I Don't Wanna Go on with You Like That">I Don't Wanna Go on with You Like That</a>", No. 2 in the US in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-12"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Charts_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Charts-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> His highest-charting single was a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Warwick" title="Dionne Warwick">Dionne Warwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gladys_Knight" title="Gladys Knight">Gladys Knight</a>, and Stevie Wonder on "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_What_Friends_Are_For" title="That's What Friends Are For">That's What Friends Are For</a>" which reached No. 1 in the US in 1985; credited as Dionne and Friends, the song raised funds for AIDS research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Charts_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Charts-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> His albums continued to sell, but of those released in the latter half of the 1980s, only <i><a href="/wiki/Reg_Strikes_Back" title="Reg Strikes Back">Reg Strikes Back</a></i> (number 16, 1988) placed in the top 20 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Charts_58-4"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Charts-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s:_.22Sacrifice.22_to_Aida_.281990.E2.80.931999.29">1990s: "Sacrifice" to <i>Aida</i> (1990–1999)</span></h3>
<p>In 1990, he achieved his first solo UK number one hit single, with "<a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_(Elton_John_song)" title="Sacrifice (Elton John song)">Sacrifice</a>" (coupled with "<a href="/wiki/Healing_Hands_(song)" title="Healing Hands (song)">Healing Hands</a>") from the previous year's album <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeping_with_the_Past" title="Sleeping with the Past">Sleeping with the Past</a></i>; it would stay at the top spot for six weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, John's "Basque" won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Instrumental_Composition" title="Grammy Award for Best Instrumental Composition">Grammy for Best Instrumental</a>, and a guest concert appearance at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a> he had made on <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>'s cover of "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Let_the_Sun_Go_Down_on_Me" title="Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me">Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me</a>" was released as a single and topped the charts in both the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies#1991" title="List of BRIT Awards ceremonies">1991</a> <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a> in London, Elton John won the award for Best British Male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1992 he released the US number 8 album <i><a href="/wiki/The_One_(Elton_John_album)" title="The One (Elton John album)">The One</a></i>, featuring the hit song "<a href="/wiki/The_One_(Elton_John_song)" title="The One (Elton John song)">The One</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> John and Taupin then signed a music publishing deal with Warner/Chappell Music for an estimated $39 million over 12 years, giving them the largest cash advance in music publishing history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1992, John appeared at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a> at Wembley Stadium, performing "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" with the remaining members of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Axl_Rose" title="Axl Rose">Axl Rose</a> of <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a> and Queen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> In September, John performed "The One" at the <a href="/wiki/1992_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1992 MTV Video Music Awards">1992 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, and also closed the ceremony performing "November Rain" with Guns N' Roses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, he released <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_(Elton_John_album)" title="Duets (Elton John album)">Duets</a></i>, a collaboration with 15 artists including <a href="/wiki/Tammy_Wynette" title="Tammy Wynette">Tammy Wynette</a> and <a href="/wiki/RuPaul" title="RuPaul">RuPaul</a>. This also included a new collaboration with Kiki Dee, entitled "True Love", which reached the Top 10 of the UK charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"For myself as well as for many others no-one has been there more for inspiration than Elton John. When we talk of great rock duos like Jimmy Page and Robert Plant, John [Lennon] and Paul [McCartney], Mick [Jagger] and Keith [Richards], I like to think of Elton John and Bernie Taupin. Also tonight I think that Elton should be honoured for his great work and contribution in the fight against AIDS. And also his bravery in exposing all the triumphs and tragedies of his personal life. "</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Axl_Rose" title="Axl Rose">Axl Rose</a> speech inducting Elton John into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a>, Elton John wrote the songs for the 1994 <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a> animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i>. At the <a href="/wiki/67th_Academy_Awards" title="67th Academy Awards">67th Academy Awards</a> ceremony, <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(soundtrack)" title="The Lion King (soundtrack)"><i>The Lion King</i> soundtrack</a> provided three of the five nominees for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Song">Academy Award for Best Song</a>, which he won with "<a href="/wiki/Can_You_Feel_the_Love_Tonight" title="Can You Feel the Love Tonight">Can You Feel the Love Tonight</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BILL_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BILL-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Both that and "<a href="/wiki/Circle_of_Life" title="Circle of Life">Circle of Life</a>" became hit songs for John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> "Can You Feel the Love Tonight" would also win Elton John the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award</a> for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/37th_Grammy_Awards" title="37th Grammy Awards">37th Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BILL_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-BILL-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> After the release of the <i>The Lion King</i> soundtrack, the album remained at the top of <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> for nine weeks. On 10 November 1999, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIAA" title="RIAA">RIAA</a> certified <i>The Lion King</i> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamond_record" title="Diamond record">Diamond</a>" for selling 15 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ELT_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-ELT-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1994, Elton John was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> by Guns N' Roses frontman <a href="/wiki/Axl_Rose" title="Axl Rose">Axl Rose</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1995 he released <i><a href="/wiki/Made_in_England_(Elton_John_album)" title="Made in England (Elton John album)">Made in England</a></i> (number 3, 1995), which featured the single "<a href="/wiki/Believe_(Elton_John_song)" title="Believe (Elton John song)">Believe</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> John performed "Believe" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies#1995" title="List of BRIT Awards ceremonies">1995</a> <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>, and picked up the prize for Outstanding Contribution to Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> A duet with <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti" title="Luciano Pavarotti">Luciano Pavarotti</a>, "Live Like Horses", reached number nine in the UK in December 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-13"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> A compilation album called <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Songs_(Elton_John_album)" title="Love Songs (Elton John album)">Love Songs</a></i> was released in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Early in 1997 he held a 50th birthday party, costumed as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, for 500 friends. He also performed with the surviving members of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> in Paris at the opening night (17 January 1997) of <i>Le Presbytère N'a Rien Perdu De Son Charme Ni Le Jardin De Son Éclat</i>, a work by French ballet legend <a href="/wiki/Maurice_B%C3%A9jart" title="Maurice Béjart">Maurice Béjart</a> which draws upon AIDS and the deaths of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> and the company's principal dancer <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Donn" title="Jorge Donn">Jorge Donn</a>. Later in 1997, two close friends died: designer <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace" title="Gianni Versace">Gianni Versace</a> was murdered; <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a> died in a Paris car crash on 31 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
