<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Most of the lyrics of "<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997</a>" were written to suit the circumstances of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>' life and death</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In early September, he contacted his writing partner <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Bernie Taupin</a>, asking him to revise the lyrics of his 1973 song "Candle in the Wind" to honour Diana, and Taupin rewrote the song accordingly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> On 6 September 1997, John performed "<a href="/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The song became the fastest and biggest-selling single of all time, eventually selling over 33 million copies worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ELT_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-ELT-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAM_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-GRAM-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> the best-selling single in UK Chart history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> the best-selling single in <i>Billboard</i> history and the only single ever <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified Diamond</a> in the United States – the single sold over 11 million copies in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSTO_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSTO-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ELT_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-ELT-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Also the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> 2009 states that the song is "the biggest-selling single since UK and US singles charts began in the 1950s, having accumulated worldwide sales of 33 million copies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guinness_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guinness-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The song proceeds of approximately £55 million were donated to the <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales_Memorial_Fund" title="Diana, Princess of Wales Memorial Fund">Diana, Princess of Wales Memorial Fund</a>. It would win Elton John the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/40th_Grammy_Awards" title="40th Grammy Awards">40th Grammy Awards</a> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAM_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-GRAM-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Something_About_the_Way_You_Look_Tonight" title="Something About the Way You Look Tonight">Something About the Way You Look Tonight</a>" was released as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_A-side" title="Double A-side">double A-side</a>. Elton John has publicly performed "Candle in the Wind 1997" only once, at Diana's funeral, vowing never to perform it again unless asked by Diana's sons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pophistorydig.com_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-pophistorydig.com-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 September 1997, Elton appeared at the <i><a href="/wiki/Music_for_Montserrat" title="Music for Montserrat">Music for Montserrat</a></i> charity concert at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, London, performing "Your Song", "Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me" and "Live Like Horses" solo before finishing with "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>" alongside fellow English artists <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 1997, Elton performed in the BBC's <a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a> charity single "<a href="/wiki/Perfect_Day_(Lou_Reed_song)#BBC_corporate_film_and_charity_release" title="Perfect Day (Lou Reed song)">Perfect Day</a>", which reached number one in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the musical theatre world, in addition to a 1998 adaptation of <i>The Lion King</i> for Broadway, he also composed music for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">Disney</a> production of <i><a href="/wiki/Aida_(musical)" title="Aida (musical)">Aida</a></i> in 1999 with lyricist <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a>, for which they received the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Tony Award for Best Original Score">Tony Award for Best Original Score</a> at the <a href="/wiki/54th_Tony_Awards" title="54th Tony Awards">54th Tony Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Musical_Show_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Musical Show Album">Grammy Award for Best Musical Show Album</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/43rd_Grammy_Awards" title="43rd Grammy Awards">43rd Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The musical was given its world premiere in the Alliance Theatre in Atlanta. It went on to Chicago and eventually Broadway. He also released a live compilation album called <i><a href="/wiki/Elton_John_One_Night_Only_%E2%80%93_The_Greatest_Hits" title="Elton John One Night Only – The Greatest Hits">Elton John One Night Only – The Greatest Hits</a></i> from the show he did at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York City that same year. A concept album from the musical titled <i><a href="/wiki/Elton_John_and_Tim_Rice%27s_Aida" title="Elton John and Tim Rice's Aida">Elton John and Tim Rice's Aida</a></i> was also released and featured the duets, "<a href="/wiki/Written_in_the_Stars_(Elton_John_and_LeAnn_Rimes_song)" title="Written in the Stars (Elton John and LeAnn Rimes song)">Written in the Stars</a>" with <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a>, and "I Know the Truth" with <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s:_Are_You_Ready_for_Love_and_60th_birthday_.282000.E2.80.932009.29">2000s: <i>Are You Ready for Love</i> and 60th birthday (2000–2009)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2593" data-file-width="2593" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg/220px-Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg/330px-Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg/440px-Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_in_Norway_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John performs at the <a href="/wiki/Skagerak_Arena" title="Skagerak Arena">Skagerak Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Skien" title="Skien">Skien</a>, Norway, June 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000, he and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a> teamed again to create songs for <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks" title="DreamWorks">DreamWorks</a>' animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Road_to_El_Dorado" title="The Road to El Dorado">The Road to El Dorado</a></i>. he released his 27th album, <i><a href="/wiki/Songs_from_the_West_Coast" title="Songs from the West Coast">Songs from the West Coast</a></i>, in October 2001. At this point, Elton John disliked appearing in his own music videos; "<a href="/wiki/This_Train_Don%27t_Stop_There_Anymore" title="This Train Don't Stop There Anymore">This Train Don't Stop There Anymore</a>" featured <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> portraying a young Elton, and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Want_Love" title="I Want Love">I Want Love</a>" featured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Downey,_Jr." title="Robert Downey, Jr.">Robert Downey, Jr.</a> lip-syncing the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_Grammy_Awards" title="2001 Grammy Awards">2001 Grammy Awards</a>, Elton performed "<a href="/wiki/Stan_(song)" title="Stan (song)">Stan</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> One month after the September 11 attacks, Elton John appeared at <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">the Concert for New York City</a>, performing "I Want Love" as well as "Your Song" in a duet with <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2003 Elton scored his fifth UK number one single when "<a href="/wiki/Are_You_Ready_for_Love" title="Are You Ready for Love">Are You Ready for Love</a>" topped the charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Returning to musical theatre, John composed music for a <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a> theatre production of <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_Elliot_the_Musical" title="Billy Elliot the Musical">Billy Elliot the Musical</a></i> in 2005 with playwright <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hall_(playwright)" title="Lee Hall (playwright)">Lee Hall</a>. Opening to strong reviews, the West End production is still running as of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> His only theatrical project with Bernie Taupin is <i><a href="/wiki/Lestat_(musical)" title="Lestat (musical)">Lestat: The Musical</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice">Anne Rice</a> vampire novels. However it received harsh reviews from critics and closed in May 2006 after 39 performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton featured on rapper <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a>'s posthumous single "<a href="/wiki/Ghetto_Gospel" title="Ghetto Gospel">Ghetto Gospel</a>", which topped the UK charts in July 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-14"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Elton John was named a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Legend" title="Disney Legend">Disney Legend</a> for his contributions to Disney's films and theatrical works on 9 October 2006, by The Walt Disney Company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006 he told <i>Rolling Stone</i> that he plans for his next record to be in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> genre. "I want to work with <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell [Williams]</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop [Lion]</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye [West]</a>, Eminem and just see what happens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6abc_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-6abc-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2007 he performed at Madison Square Garden for a record breaking 60th time for his 60th birthday, the concert was broadcast live and a DVD recording was released as <i><a href="/wiki/Elton_60_%E2%80%93_Live_at_Madison_Square_Garden" title="Elton 60 – Live at Madison Square Garden">Elton 60 – Live at Madison Square Garden</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> a greatest-hits compilation CD, <i>Rocket Man – Number Ones</i>, was released in 17 different versions worldwide, including a CD/DVD combo; and his back catalogue – almost 500 songs from 32 albums – became available for legal download.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/220px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/330px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/440px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton on piano at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a>, commemorating <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Princess Diana</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> on 1 July 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 1 July 2007, Elton John appeared at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a> held at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in London, in honour of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>, on what would have been her 46th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diana_Concert_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diana_Concert-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> John opened the concert with "Your Song", and then closed the concert with his second performance, with "Saturday Night's Alright For Fighting", "Tiny Dancer", and "Are You Ready For Love".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diana_Concert_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Diana_Concert-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a September 2008 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> magazine, John said: "I'm going on the road again with <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a> again next year," referring to "Face to Face," a series of concerts featuring both musicians. The tour began in March and will continue for at least two more years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2003, he announced that he had signed an exclusive agreement to perform 75 shows over three years at <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Strip" title="Las Vegas Strip">Las Vegas Strip</a>. The show, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Red_Piano" title="The Red Piano">The Red Piano</a></i>, was a multimedia concert featuring massive props and video montages created by <a href="/wiki/David_LaChapelle" title="David LaChapelle">David LaChapelle</a>. Effectively, he and <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a> share performances at Caesars Palace throughout the year – while one performs, one rests. The first of these shows took place on 13 February 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2006, Elton and Dion sang together at the venue to raise money for Harrah's Entertainment Inc. workers affected by the 2005 hurricanes, performing "Sorry Seems to Be the Hardest Word" and "Saturday Night's Alright (for Fighting)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> On 21 June 2008, Elton performed his 200th show in Caesars Palace. A DVD/CD package of <i>The Red Piano</i> was released through Best Buy in November 2008. A two-year global tour was sandwiched between commitments in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, Nevada, some of the venues of which were new to John. The Red Piano Tour closed in Las Vegas in April 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.93present">2010–present</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_(8183493581).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1000" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg/220px-Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg/330px-Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg/440px-Elton_John_%288183493581%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_(8183493581).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton on <a href="/wiki/World_AIDS_Day" title="World AIDS Day">World AIDS Day</a> in Sydney, Australia on 1 December 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Elton John performed a piano duet with <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/52nd_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Grammy Awards">52nd Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> On 6 June 2010, John performed at the fourth wedding of conservative commentator <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a> for a reported US$1 million fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Eleven days later, and 17 years to the day after his last previous performance in Israel, he performed at the <a href="/wiki/Ramat_Gan_Stadium" title="Ramat Gan Stadium">Ramat Gan Stadium</a>; this was significant because of other then-recent cancellations by other performers in the fallout surrounding an <a href="/wiki/Gaza_flotilla_raid" title="Gaza flotilla raid">Israeli raid</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ships_of_the_Gaza_flotilla_raid" title="Ships of the Gaza flotilla raid">Gaza Flotilla</a> the month before. In his introduction to that concert, Elton John noted he and other musicians should not "cherry-pick our conscience", in reference to <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Costello" title="Elvis Costello">Elvis Costello</a>, who was to have performed in Israel two weeks after John did, but cancelled in the wake of the aforementioned raid, citing his [Costello's] conscience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Union_(Elton_John_and_Leon_Russell_album)" title="The Union (Elton John and Leon Russell album)">The Union</a></i> on 19 October 2010. John says his collaboration with American singer, songwriter and sideman <a href="/wiki/Leon_Russell" title="Leon Russell">Leon Russell</a> marks a new chapter in his recording career, saying: "I don't have to make pop records any more."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He began his new show <a href="/wiki/The_Million_Dollar_Piano" title="The Million Dollar Piano">The Million Dollar Piano</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Colosseum_at_Caesars_Palace" title="The Colosseum at Caesars Palace">The Colosseum</a> at <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a>, Las Vegas on 28 September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> John will be performing the show at Caesars for the next three years. He performed his 3000th concert on Saturday 8 October 2011 at Caesars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, John performed vocals on <i>Snowed in at Wheeler Street</i> with <a href="/wiki/Kate_Bush" title="Kate Bush">Kate Bush</a> for her <i><a href="/wiki/50_Words_for_Snow" title="50 Words for Snow">50 Words for Snow</a></i> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> On 3 February 2012, Elton John visited Costa Rica for the first time when he performed at the recently built <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Nacional_de_Costa_Rica_(2011)" title="Estadio Nacional de Costa Rica (2011)">National Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 June 2012, he performed at the Queen's <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_Concert" title="Diamond Jubilee Concert">Diamond Jubilee Concert</a> at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, performing a repertoire including "Your Song", "Crocodile Rock" and "I'm Still Standing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> On 30 June, John performed in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, Ukraine at a joint concert with <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> + <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> for the Elena Pinchuk ANTIAIDS Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>An album containing remixes of songs that he recorded in the 1970s called <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_to_the_Night" title="Good Morning to the Night">Good Morning to the Night</a></i> was released in July 2012. The remixes were conducted by Australian group <a href="/wiki/Pnau" title="Pnau">Pnau</a> and the album reached No. 1 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Pride_of_Britain_Awards" title="Pride of Britain Awards">Pride of Britain Awards</a> on 30 October, Elton John, along with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a>, recited <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Rudyard Kipling</a>'s poem "<a href="/wiki/If%E2%80%94" title="If—">If—</a>" in tribute to the 2012 British <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the 2012 Summer Olympics">Olympic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="Great Britain at the 2012 Summer Paralympics">Paralympics</a> athletes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2013, Elton performed a duet with singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/55th_Grammy_Awards" title="55th Grammy Awards">55th Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in 2013 he collaborated with rock band <a href="/wiki/Queens_of_the_Stone_Age" title="Queens of the Stone Age">Queens of the Stone Age</a> on their sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/...Like_Clockwork" title="...Like Clockwork">...Like Clockwork</a></i>, contributing piano and vocals on the song "Fairweather Friends". He stated that he was a fan of frontman <a href="/wiki/Josh_Homme" title="Josh Homme">Josh Homme</a>'s side project, <a href="/wiki/Them_Crooked_Vultures" title="Them Crooked Vultures">Them Crooked Vultures</a>, and had contacted Homme via phone call, asking if he could perform on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2013, Elton received the first <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brits Icon Award</a> for his "lasting impact" on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">UK Culture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Icon_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Icon-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a> presented him the award on stage at the <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a> before the two performed a duet of "Sad Songs (Say So Much)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> It had been announced in March 2012 that John had completed work on his thirty-first album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diving_Board" title="The Diving Board">The Diving Board</a></i>. The album was produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-Bone_Burnett" title="T-Bone Burnett">T-Bone Burnett</a> and was originally set for release in autumn 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's release date was pushed back multiple times, but on its release in September 2013 it reached No. 3 in the UK and No. 4 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charts_35-15"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songwriting">Songwriting</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="959" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG/230px-Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG/345px-Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG/460px-Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_Bernie_Taupin_1971.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elton John with <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Bernie Taupin</a> (left) in 1971</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>John has written with his songwriting partner <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Taupin" title="Bernie Taupin">Bernie Taupin</a> since 1967 when he answered an advertisement for talent placed in the popular UK music publication, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Musical_Express" title="New Musical Express">New Musical Express</a></i>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberty_records" title="Liberty records">Liberty records</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%26R" title="A&amp;R">A&amp;R</a> man <a href="/wiki/Ray_Williams_(producer)" title="Ray Williams (producer)">Ray Williams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair have collaborated on more than 30 albums to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 1991 film documentary <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two_Rooms" title="Two Rooms">Two Rooms</a></i> described the writing style that Elton John and Bernie Taupin use, which involves Taupin writing the lyrics on his own, and John then putting them to music, with the two never in the same room during the process. Taupin would write a set of lyrics, then mail them to John, wherever he was in the world, who would then lay down the music, arrange it, and record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992 he was inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songwriter%27s_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriter's Hall of Fame">Songwriter's Hall of Fame</a>. John is a fellow of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a> (BASCA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basca.org.uk_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Basca.org.uk-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<p>Elton John's voice was once classed as <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a>; it is now <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenthal_22-11"><a href="#cite_note-Rosenthal-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> His piano playing is influenced by <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> He used <a href="/wiki/Paul_Buckmaster" title="Paul Buckmaster">Paul Buckmaster</a> to arrange the music on his studio albums during the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexuality_and_family">Sexuality and family</span></h3>
<p>In the late 1960s, Elton John was engaged to be married to his first lover, secretary Linda Woodrow, who is mentioned in the song "<a href="/wiki/Someone_Saved_My_Life_Tonight" title="Someone Saved My Life Tonight">Someone Saved My Life Tonight</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS76_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS76-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myers_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Myers-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> He married German recording engineer Renate Blauel on 14 February 1984, in <a href="/wiki/Darling_Point,_New_South_Wales" title="Darling Point, New South Wales">Darling Point</a>, Sydney, with speculation that the marriage was a <a href="/wiki/Beard_(companion)" title="Beard (companion)">cover</a> for his homosexuality. John came out as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a> in a 1976 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS76_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-RS76-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myers_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-Myers-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> but after his divorce from Blauel in 1988, he told the magazine that he was "comfortable" being gay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, he began a relationship with <a href="/wiki/David_Furnish" title="David Furnish">David Furnish</a>, a former advertising executive and now filmmaker originally from <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Canada. On 21 December 2005 (the day that the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Partnership_Act_2004" title="Civil Partnership Act 2004">Civil Partnership Act</a> came into force), John and Furnish were amongst the first couples in the UK to form a <a href="/wiki/Civil_partnership_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Civil partnership in the United Kingdom">civil partnership</a>, which was held at the <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Guildhall" title="Windsor Guildhall">Windsor Guildhall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_marriage" title="Gay marriage">gay marriage</a> became legal in England in March 2014, John and Furnish married in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor, Berkshire</a> on 21 December 2014, the ninth anniversary of their civil partnership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> They have two sons. Their oldest, Zachary Jackson Levon Furnish-John, was born to a surrogate mother on 25 December 2010 in California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> A second son, Elijah Joseph Daniel Furnish-John, was born to the couple by the same surrogate mother on 11 January 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Elton John has ten known godchildren, including <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">Sean Lennon</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Beckham" title="Victoria Beckham">Victoria Beckham</a>'s sons Brooklyn and Romeo, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Hurley" title="Elizabeth Hurley">Elizabeth Hurley</a>'s son Damian Charles, and the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Stein" title="Seymour Stein">Seymour Stein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warren_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>John was a staunch supporter of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Same-sex marriage in the United Kingdom">same-sex marriage in the United Kingdom</a> and argued in 2012: "There is a world of difference between calling someone your 'partner' and calling them your 'husband'. 'Partner' is a word that should be preserved for people you play tennis with, or work alongside in business. It doesn't come close to describing the love that I have for David, and he for me. In contrast, 'husband' does."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, he addressed the religious perspective on sexuality, claiming Jesus would have been in favour of homosexual marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Elton John resisted calls to boycott Russia in protest at the country's anti-gay legislation, but told fans at a Moscow concert that the Russian laws were "inhumane and isolating" and he was "deeply saddened and shocked over the current legislation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> In a January 2014 interview, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> spoke of Elton John in an attempt to show that there was no gay discrimination in Russia, stating; "Elton John – he's an extraordinary person, a distinguished musician, and millions of our people sincerely love him, regardless of his sexual orientation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Russia-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton responded by offering to introduce the President to Russians abused under Russian legislation banning "homosexual propaganda".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russia_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Russia-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth">Wealth</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_on_stage,_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="667" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg/170px-Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg/255px-Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg/340px-Elton_John_on_stage%2C_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elton_John_on_stage,_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
John on stage in July 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In April 2009, the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Sunday Times Rich List</a></i> estimated John's wealth to be £175 million (US$265 million), and ranked him as the 322nd wealthiest person in Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> John was estimated to have a fortune of £195 million in the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Sunday Times Rich List</a></i> of 2011, making him one of the 10 wealthiest people in the British music industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> Aside from his main home "Woodside" in <a href="/wiki/Old_Windsor" title="Old Windsor">Old Windsor</a>, Berkshire, John owns residences in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, Nice, London's <a href="/wiki/Holland_Park" title="Holland Park">Holland Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. John's property in Nice is based on Mon Boron mountain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> Elton John is an art collector, and is believed to have one of the largest private photography collections in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, he admitted to spending £30 million in just under two years—an average of £1.5 million a month. Between January 1996 and September 1997, he spent more than £9.6m on property and £293,000 on flowers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2001 John sold 20 of his cars at <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie's">Christie's</a>, saying he didn't get the chance to drive them because he was out of the country so often.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> The sale, which included a 1993 <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_XJ220" title="Jaguar XJ220">Jaguar XJ220</a>, the most expensive at £234,750, and several <a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferraris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Limited" title="Rolls-Royce Limited">Rolls-Royces</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">Bentleys</a>, raised nearly £2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, John sold the contents of his Holland Park home—expected to fetch £800,000 at <a href="/wiki/Sotheby%27s" title="Sotheby's">Sotheby's</a>—in a bid to create more room for his collection of contemporary art which includes many works of art by <a href="/wiki/Young_British_Artists" title="Young British Artists">Young British Artists</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sam_Taylor-Wood" title="Sam Taylor-Wood">Sam Taylor-Wood</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tracy_Emin" title="Tracy Emin">Tracy Emin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> Every year since 2004, John has opened a shop called "Elton's Closet" in which he sells his second-hand clothes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span></h3>
<p>By 1975, the pressures of stardom had begun to take a serious toll on him. During "Elton Week" in Los Angeles that year, he suffered a drug overdose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> He also battled the eating disorder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulimia" title="Bulimia">bulimia</a>. In a CNN interview with <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a> in 2002, King asked if John knew of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>' eating disorder. John replied, "Yes, I did. We were both bulimic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A longtime tennis enthusiast, he wrote the song "Philadelphia Freedom" in tribute to long-time friend <a href="/wiki/Billie_Jean_King" title="Billie Jean King">Billie Jean King</a> and her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Team_Tennis" title="World Team Tennis">World Team Tennis</a> franchise of the same name. John and King also co-host an annual pro-am event to benefit AIDS charities, most notably Elton John's own <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a>, for which King is a chairwoman. John, who maintains a part-time residence in Atlanta, Georgia, became a fan of the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> baseball team when he moved there in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2015, he was named one of <a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a>'s 50 best dressed British men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Watford_Football_Club">Watford Football Club</span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:26%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"At the 1984 Cup Final, the song "<a href="/wiki/Abide_with_Me" title="Abide with Me">Abide with Me</a>" was played and that's why I cried. The song evokes my memory of childhood."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Elton John on his emotions during the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a>'s traditional pre-match hymn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Having supported <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watford_Football_Club" title="Watford Football Club">Watford Football Club</a> since growing up locally, Elton John became the club's chairman and director in 1976, appointing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graham_Taylor_(footballer)" title="Graham Taylor (footballer)">Graham Taylor</a> as manager and investing large sums of money as the club rose three divisions into the <a href="/wiki/Football_in_England" title="Football in England">English</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> The pinnacle of the club's success was finishing runners up in the First Division to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool F.C.</a> in 1983 and reaching the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> in 1984. He sold the club to <a href="/wiki/Jack_Petchey" title="Jack Petchey">Jack Petchey</a> in 1987, but remained their lifelong president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAT_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-WAT-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, he re-purchased the club from Petchey and once again became chairman. He stepped down in 2002 when the club needed a full-time chairman although he continued as president of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAT_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-WAT-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> Although no longer the majority shareholder, he still holds a significant financial interest. In June 2005 he held a concert at Watford's <a href="/wiki/Vicarage_Road" title="Vicarage Road">Vicarage Road</a>, donating the funds to the club, and another concert in May 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAT_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-WAT-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> He has remained friends with a number of high profile players in football including <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warren_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> For a time, between late 1975 – 1976, he was a part-owner of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Aztecs" title="Los Angeles Aztecs">Los Angeles Aztecs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League" title="North American Soccer League">North American Soccer League</a>. On 13 December 2014, he attended Vicarage road with David Furnish, and his sons Zachary and Elijah for the opening of the "Sir Elton John stand", He described the day as "one of the greatest days of my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="AIDS_Foundation">AIDS Foundation</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a></div>
<p>Elton John has been associated with AIDS charities since the deaths of his friends <a href="/wiki/Ryan_White" title="Ryan White">Ryan White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, raising large amounts of money and using his public profile to raise awareness of the disease. For example, in 1986 he joined with <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Warwick" title="Dionne Warwick">Dionne Warwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gladys_Knight" title="Gladys Knight">Gladys Knight</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a> to record the single "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_What_Friends_Are_For" title="That's What Friends Are For">That's What Friends Are For</a>", with all profits being donated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Foundation_for_AIDS_Research" title="American Foundation for AIDS Research">American Foundation for AIDS Research</a>. The song won John and the others the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocals" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals">Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals</a>. In April 1990, Elton performed his 1968 ballad "<a href="/wiki/Skyline_Pigeon" title="Skyline Pigeon">Skyline Pigeon</a>" at the funeral of White, a teenage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haemophiliac" title="Haemophiliac">haemophiliac</a> he had befriended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He founded the <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a> in 1992 as a charity to fund programmes for HIV/AIDS prevention, for the elimination of prejudice and discrimination against HIV/AIDS-affected individuals, and for providing services to people living with or at risk of contracting HIV/AIDS. This cause continues to be one of his personal passions. In 1993 he began hosting his annual <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation_Academy_Award_Party" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation Academy Award Party">Academy Award Party</a>, which has become one of the highest-profile Oscar parties in the Hollywood film industry, and has raised over $200 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foundation_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Foundation-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 2006, John donated the smaller of two bright-red <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yamaha_(manufacturer)" title="Yamaha (manufacturer)">Yamaha</a> pianos from his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, Nevada show to auction on eBay to raise public awareness and funds for the foundation.</p>
<p>To raise money for his AIDS charity, he annually hosts a glamorous White Tie &amp; Tiara Ball In the grounds of his home in <a href="/wiki/Old_Windsor" title="Old Windsor">Old Windsor</a>, Berkshire to which many famous celebrities are invited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ball_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ball-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> On 28 June 2007, the 9th annual White Tie &amp; Tiara Ball took place. The menu consisted of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuber_(genus)" title="Tuber (genus)">truffle</a> <a href="/wiki/Souffl%C3%A9" title="Soufflé">soufflé</a> followed by Surf and Turf (<a href="/wiki/Filet_mignon" title="Filet mignon">filet mignon</a> with <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a> tail) and a giant <a href="/wiki/Knickerbocker_glory" title="Knickerbocker glory">Knickerbocker glory</a> ice cream. An auction followed the dinner held by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a>. A Rolls Royce 'Phantom' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drophead" title="Drophead">drophead</a> coupe and a piece of <a href="/wiki/Tracey_Emin" title="Tracey Emin">Tracey Emin</a>'s artwork both raised £800,000 for the charity fund, with the total amount raised reaching £3.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, Elton sang "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delilah_(1968_song)" title="Delilah (1968 song)">Delilah</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Tom_Jones_(singer)" title="Tom Jones (singer)">Tom Jones</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Big_Spender" title="Big Spender">Big Spender</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Bassey" title="Shirley Bassey">Shirley Bassey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2011 guests included <a href="/wiki/Sarah,_Duchess_of_York" title="Sarah, Duchess of York">Sarah, Duchess of York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Hurley" title="Elizabeth Hurley">Elizabeth Hurley</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> (who performed "Don't Let the Sun Go Down on Me" in a duet with Elton), and the auction raised £5 million, adding to the £45 million the Balls have raised for the Elton John Aids Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ball_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ball-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_awards">Honours and awards</span></h2>
<p>He was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in his first year of eligibility in 1994. He and Bernie Taupin had previously been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> in 1992. John was appointed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> For his charitable work, John was <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a> on 24 February 1998. In October 1975, John became the 1,662nd person to receive a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HWOF_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-HWOF-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He became a recipient of a <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honor</a> in 2004, and a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Legends" title="Disney Legends">Disney Legends</a> Award in 2006. In 2010, he was awarded with the <a href="/wiki/PRS_for_Music" title="PRS for Music">PRS for Music</a> <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Award" title="Heritage Award">Heritage Award</a>, which was erected, on The Namaste Lounge Pub in Watford, where John performed his first ever gig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Music awards include the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a> for "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Can_You_Feel_The_Love_Tonight" title="Can You Feel The Love Tonight">Can You Feel The Love Tonight</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i> (award shared with Tim Rice); the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song</a> in 1994 for "Can You Feel The Love Tonight" from <i>The Lion King</i> (award shared with Tim Rice); and the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Tony Award for Best Original Score">Tony Award for Best Original Score</a> in 2000 for <a href="/wiki/Aida_(musical)" title="Aida (musical)"><i>Elton John and Tim Rice's Aida</i></a> (award shared with Tim Rice). He has also received five <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>, including the award for Best British Male in 1991, awards for Outstanding Contribution to Music in 1986 and 1995, and in 2013 the first Brits Icon award in recognition of his "lasting impact" on UK culture presented to him by his close friend <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Icon_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Icon-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_awards">Film awards</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy_Awards"><a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a></span></h4>
<ol>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> (<b>won</b>) for <i><a href="/wiki/Can_You_Feel_the_Love_Tonight" title="Can You Feel the Love Tonight">Can You Feel the Love Tonight</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> (nominated) for <i><a href="/wiki/Circle_of_Life" title="Circle of Life">Circle of Life</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> (nominated) for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hakuna_Matata" title="Hakuna Matata">Hakuna Matata</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_awards">Music awards</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammy_Awards"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a></span></h4>
<ol>
<li>1972: Grammy Award for Best Original Score Written for a Motion Picture (nominated) for <i><a href="/wiki/Friends_(1971_film)" title="Friends (1971 film)">Friends</a></i></li>
<li>1987: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal" title="Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal">Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal</a> (<b>won</b>) for "That's What Friends Are For", performed by Dionne Warwick &amp; Friends (award shared with Dionne Warwick, Gladys Knight &amp; Stevie Wonder)</li>
<li>1991: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Instrumental_Composition" title="Best Instrumental Composition">Best Instrumental Composition</a> (<b>won</b>) for "Basque", performed by James Galway</li>
<li>1994: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a> for "Can You Feel The Love Tonight"</li>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a> (<b>won</b>) for <i><a href="/wiki/Can_You_Feel_the_Love_Tonight" title="Can You Feel the Love Tonight">Can You Feel the Love Tonight</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media">Best Song Written Specifically for a Motion Picture or for Television</a> (nominated) for <i><a href="/wiki/Can_You_Feel_the_Love_Tonight" title="Can You Feel the Love Tonight">Can You Feel the Love Tonight</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
<li>1995: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media">Best Song Written Specifically for a Motion Picture or for Television</a> (nominated) for <i><a href="/wiki/Circle_of_Life" title="Circle of Life">Circle of Life</a></i> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King" title="The Lion King">The Lion King</a></i></li>
<li>1997: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a> (<b>won</b>) for "Candle in the Wind 1997"</li>
<li>1999: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Legend_Award" title="Grammy Legend Award">Grammy Legend Award</a></li>
<li>2001: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Musical_Show_Album" title="Best Musical Show Album">Best Musical Show Album</a> (<b>won</b>) for <i>Elton John &amp; Tim Rice's Aida</i> (award shared with <a href="/wiki/Guy_Babylon" title="Guy Babylon">Guy Babylon</a>, Paul Bogaev &amp; Chris Montan (producers), <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a> (lyricist) and the original Broadway cast with <a href="/wiki/Heather_Headley" title="Heather Headley">Heather Headley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Pascal" title="Adam Pascal">Adam Pascal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sherie_Rene_Scott" title="Sherie Rene Scott">Sherie Rene Scott</a>)</li>
<li>2011: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Pop_Collaboration_with_Vocals" title="Best Pop Collaboration with Vocals">Best Pop Collaboration with Vocals</a> (nominated) for If it Wasn't for Bad</li>
</ol>

</ol>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg/220px-Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg/330px-Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg/440px-Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rlton_John_Band_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Elton John Band 15 March 2012 Left to Right: John, Johnstone, Birch, and (not pictured, right), Olsson and Cooper</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1970, John's band, of which he is the pianist and lead singer, has been known as the Elton John Band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> The band has had multiple line-up changes, but <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Olsson" title="Nigel Olsson">Nigel Olsson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnstone" title="Davey Johnstone">Davey Johnstone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ray_Cooper" title="Ray Cooper">Ray Cooper</a> have been members (albeit non-consecutively) since 1969 (Olsson) and 1972 (Johnstone and Cooper). Olsson left the band in 1984 but rejoined in 2000 .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Ray Cooper has worked on and off with the Elton John Band because he maintains obligations to other musicians as a <a href="/wiki/Session_musician" title="Session musician">session player</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sideman" title="Sideman">sideman</a> as a road-tour percussionist.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>
